Shanghai-Minhang Buses Increase Fares

▲Full Fare Six Jiao ▲ The Shanghai-Minhang-Nanzhe long-distance bus service operating between Shanghai and Minhang was taken over by the Communications Company last year. The original full fare was eight jiao. During the trial lease period, a temporary discount of 30% was applied, resulting in a fare of seven jiao. Recently, due to the continued increase in the cost of gasoline and other materials, it has become difficult to maintain the concession, so the fares have been slightly changed to 1.5 jiao from the Shanghai station to Tushan Bay, with an additional five fen added for each subsequent station. The full fare from the Shanghai station to Minhang is six jiao. This has been submitted to the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau for approval. The bureau considered that the route is 31 kilometers long and the current full fare of six jiao is less than two fen per kilometer. Moreover, considering the original fare of eight jiao, which is already low, and that the increase from the 30% discount fare of 5.8 jiao is minimal, they reported the matter to the municipal government. The government has approved the plan.

Beihui County Road Nearing Completion

Since the resumption of work on the Songhu-Beihui County Road on the 16th of this month, the recruited laborers have been very enthusiastic, resulting in rapid progress. The road has already been built to the twelfth section, with only the thirteenth and fourteenth sections remaining. It is expected to be completed and accepted by next Saturday. Director Wu of the County Construction Bureau plans to gather the heads of each section after acceptance for a segment-by-segment inspection. Any imperfections will be immediately rectified in order to ensure perfection.

Workers After the Steel Plant Shutdown

▲Meeting to Discuss Maintaining Livelihood▲ More than 400 workers at the Shanghai Steel Plant have been affected by the recent resignation of Director Hu Shuhua, the non-arrival of the new director Zhou Zhihong, and the inability to sell products, leading to a financial crisis. Although work has been temporarily suspended, the livelihoods of hundreds of workers have been affected. Therefore, the 29th sub-branch of the First District Party Branch of the plant convened the fifteenth party member meeting the day before yesterday to discuss ways to maintain livelihoods. The key resolutions were: (1) to petition the superior party organization to request the National Government to order all ordnance factories in the country to uniformly adopt the plant's steel materials; (2) to question the Shanghai Ordnance Factory for refusing to use the steel plant's steel materials and to send representatives to petition the superior party organization for relief within the next few days.

Local News

The "Daredevil" Movie Starring Rock

Contains Insults to Chinese People ▲ The Audience at the Grand Theater is Very Dissatisfied ▲ Hong Shen Speaks Out Against the Absurdity of the Film ▲ The Crowd Immediately Leaves and Demands Refunds ▲ The Film Censorship Committee Works to Ban the Film ▲ The "Daredevil" sound film starring Rock, produced by Paramount Pictures, which recently began showing at the Grand Theater on Jing'an Temple Road, has been doing well at the box office. However, the film contains backgrounds such as Cantonese people and Chinatown, and the subject matter is absurd, which is very offensive to Chinese people. During the 5:30 PM showing yesterday, the audience was very dissatisfied because it considered the film to be extremely insulting to Chinese people. At that time, Hong Shen, a drama professor at Fudan University, spoke out against the absurdity of the film, and the crowd joined in, leaving and demanding refunds of more than 300 tickets. During the chaos, the audience questioned the Western manager, causing some disorder. After receiving the news, the New Zha Police Department immediately sent Chinese and foreign detectives to suppress the situation, which was quickly calmed down. Hong Shen also went to the police station to explain everything and left.

In addition, the Shanghai Special City Film Censorship Committee believes that the "Daredevil" film starring Rock, which is being shown at the Grand Theater and the Guanglu Theater, completely insults Chinese people. The committee believes that the two theaters are showing this type of film despite public anger, which is outrageous. The ad hoc committee resolved the following: (1) to warn the two theaters; (2) to submit a request to the municipal government to negotiate seriously with the American Consul; (3) to publish advertisements warning Chinese people not to watch the film again; (4) to order all theaters not to show the film again.

Gunfight on Xinjiang Road Last Night

Bandits Resist Arrest and Open Fire ▲ Stray Bullet Kills One and Wounds One ▲ It is Unknown Whether the Deceased Was a Bandit ▲ Around 7:30 PM last night, bandits resisted arrest and opened fire at the intersection of Xinjiang Road and Wuzhen Road in Zhabei, killing one person and wounding one rickshaw puller. One principal offender and three suspects were apprehended on the spot by Zhabei detectives from the Public Security Bureau. The details are as follows: ▲Informant's Report ▲ Qiao Songsheng, the captain of the detective team of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, recently ordered all detectives to step up precautions due to the unrest in the area. Yesterday evening, Wang Shifu, the leader of the Zhabei Public Security Bureau's detective team, received a report from an informant that five or six bandits were gathering in a small teahouse west of the fire station on Xinmin Road, carrying guns and weapons. Leader Wang immediately led detectives Su Sheng, Dou Yulin, Lu Xingchun, Hua Yingzhou, Wang Zijun, and others, fully armed, to Xinmin Road to investigate and apprehend them. ▲Bandits Resist Arrest ▲ The detectives rushed to the small teahouse on Xinmin Road, but the bandits had already fled after hearing the news. They were then led by the informant to Xinjiang Road, near Wuzhen Road, where they found the bandits coming from the east. They immediately ordered them to stop and submit to a search. The bandits, seeing that the situation was unfavorable, immediately drew their guns and opened fire to resist arrest. The detectives returned fire, and the two sides exchanged fire for at least seven or eight shots. The bandits, numbering about five or six, seeing that they were outnumbered, fled in different directions. One bandit was apprehended on the spot by the detectives, along with a gun and three bullets, and taken to the police station. In addition, three suspects were also apprehended. ▲One Killed and One Wounded ▲ After the gunfire stopped, one person was found lying motionless on the street, wearing a blue cloth robe and a melon-skin cap. The person had been shot twice, both times in vital areas. However, it is still unclear whether the deceased was a bandit or a passerby. At the time of the shooting, a rickshaw puller named Qian Wancheng was passing through the area and was struck in the abdomen by a stray bullet, sustaining serious injuries. He was taken by police car to the district office and then transferred to Baolong Hospital for treatment. His rickshaw number was 2285. ▲Four Apprehended ▲ A total of four people were apprehended by the detectives. One of them was the principal offender named Zhang Bin (also known as Xu Jianwu), 29 years old, from Anhui, living in the Huafeng Workshop in Wusong, working in a sugar factory. The three suspects were Zhu Jun, 26 years old, from Yancheng, living in a bungalow in Zhabei, Pubei, selling fruit; Zhou Yuetao, 31 years old, from Yancheng, living at No. 22 Yongxing Lane, Nanmatou, working as a rickshaw puller; and Zhang Yuetong, 33 years old, from Funing, living in the Xu Family Residence on Qiujiang Road, the owner of the Longxing Tea Garden.

▲From 5:45 PM to 10:30 PM ▲ Lights Not Visible Beyond 50 Steps ▲ The weather in Shanghai yesterday morning was hot and dry, especially at noon. Steamed Bone Examination Case

There is Talk of Another Appeal ▲ Yesterday's Trial at the District Court ▲ No Plaintiff Appeared ▲ The Deceased Suffered Greatly Before Death ▲ Its Root Cause Was Superstition The remains of Chen Xun (née Sun Genbao), daughter-in-law of the late Chen Shuangxi, a wealthy man from Jiangbei outside Suzhou's Changmen, have been confirmed by the Shanghai District Court's steamed bone examination to be a case of hanging suicide. Details were reported in yesterday's newspaper. After the examination, Prosecutor Yang instructed both parties to appear at the court at 2 PM the next day (yesterday) for questioning. Yesterday afternoon, the defendants all complied and reported as instructed, while no one from the plaintiff's side appeared. Subsequently, Prosecutor Yang briefly questioned the defendants and ordered them to leave, pending further review by higher authorities. However, it is heard that the plaintiff's side is preparing to appeal again. It is said that the deceased suffered abuse before her death. The origin of the abuse was that shortly after the deceased married into the family, two of her nephews died young. The Chen family was deeply superstitious and believed that the deceased's birth year and date contained great misfortune, which was detrimental to the Chen family. They also suspected that the woman's family coveted the Chen family's wealth, so they changed the deceased's birth year and date during the marriage arrangements. The Chen family did not notice and rashly arranged the marriage. After the death of the two children, the Chen family hated the deceased as an ominous object and abuse began. On the afternoon of the seventeenth day of the third month of the lunar calendar last year, at about 4 PM, the deceased died. During the initial examination by the Wu County Court the next day, the deceased had injuries all over her body, which was also a result of the poison of superstition.

Yi County Youths in Shanghai

Involved in Lawsuit Due to Literary Dispute ▲ Yi Society and Inspirational Society Incompatible ▲ Wang Liwu Files Criminal Charges ▲ Yu, Hu, and Chen Also File Counter-Suit ▲ Both Parties Found Not Guilty Yu Jie'an, Hu Xiehou, Chen Moruo, and others, natives of Yi County, Anhui Province, living in Shanghai, formed the Yi Society and published a journal called "Yi Sound Report," edited by Chen, with Yu serving as the Director of the General Affairs Department and Hu as the Director of the Accounting Department. Wang Liwu, also from Yi County, held an important position in the Yi Mountain Youth Inspirational Society in Shanghai, which also published a journal called "Yi Mountain Youth Monthly," edited by Wang. Although these two groups shared the same hometown name, they were like Qin and Yue, constantly attacking each other in newspapers, leading to a heated literary war. Recently, they became involved in a lawsuit. Wang first filed criminal charges against Yu, Hu, and Chen in the Provisional Court for defamation, claiming that the defendants published false facts and defamatory language in the first, second, third, and fourth issues of the "Yi Sound Report," accusing the plaintiff of "swindling and exploiting for personal gain," and stating that the plaintiff "uses this group as a tool for his speculative profit-making," etc., deliberately insulting him. The plaintiff works in the press and has authored many books and newspapers, and plans to establish a printing house. The defendants' false accusations damage his reputation, infringing on the plaintiff's legal rights. Therefore, he requests the court to summon the defendants to the court and punish them according to Article 325, paragraph 2, or Article 330 of the criminal law, and also requests incidental private prosecution to compensate for all losses. The defendants jointly retained lawyer Chen Tingrui to file a defense. The main points of their defense are divided into two parts: (1) Yu Jie'an and Hu Xiehou are not editors of the "Yi Sound Report." Even if the report does contain damage to reputation or public insults, Yu and Hu are not responsible in any way. (2) Although Chen Moruo is the editor of the "Yi Sound Report," the author is responsible for the words that the plaintiff claims to be damaging to reputation and publicly insulting. Even if Chen is responsible for the articles published in "Yi Sound Report," whether or not he bears criminal responsibility depends on whether the words published in "Yi Sound Report" violate Article 325, paragraph 2, and Article 330 of the criminal law. Whether or not those articles violate each of those criminal articles depends on three points for research: (A) The "Yi Sound Report" said that the plaintiff "swindles and exploits for personal gain" and "uses this group as a tool for his speculative profit-making," etc. These words are based on the request of Pan Dingyuan et al. at the 32nd regular meeting of the Shanghai Guidance Committee published in the Shanghai Central Daily on August 19, 1928, and the request of Zhang Chaoren et al. On August 6, 1928, the Times published news about the disciplinary action against Wang Liwu by the Party Training students. On December 3, 1929, the News published Announcement No. 62 of the Shanghai Special City Executive Committee of the Chinese Nationalist Party, and the Shanghai Special City Party Affairs Guidance Committee pointed to Announcement No. 15, as well as Wang Liwu's business cards and letters from comrades in various places, which are sufficient to prove the plaintiff's "swindling and exploiting for personal gain" and "using the group as a tool for speculative profit-making" are true. These facts are related to the public interest, so according to Article 326 of the Criminal Law, even if defamation is involved, there is no penalty. (B) The resolution of the 49th regular meeting of the Shanghai Special City Executive Committee of the Chinese Nationalist Party stated that party members who have been expelled from the party should not be elected as officials of various people's organizations. Announcement No. 62 also stated that this was to prevent problems from the start. However, the plaintiff, by exploiting connections, became an important official of the Yi Mountain Youth Inspirational Society and published the "Yi Mountain Youth Monthly," wantonly attacking the party, government, and all sectors of Yi County. His violation of the Kuomintang resolution to engage in speculative profit-making is very obvious. The "Yi Sound Report" is responsible for guiding the people of Yi County and fully exposing this darkness to prevent the people from being deceived, which is in line with Article 327, paragraph 3, of the Criminal Law. In the "Answering Questions from Guests for Yi Society" published in the "Yi Mountain Youth Monthly" on November 8, 1929, the plaintiff stated that "the spirit of Yi Sound is not pure," and also stated that "within the Yi Society, there are not a few local tyrants, evil gentry, corrupt officials, academic scoundrels, and degenerate youths mixed in," and also stated that the people of Yi Society are "despicable and lowly." Therefore, Hu Lichuan's article "Wang Liwu of Thousand Changes" in the "Yi Sound" is purely for self-defense, which is in line with Article 327, paragraph 1, of the Criminal Law. (C) The statements of the "Yi Sound Report" are, as described in item A, completely true facts, and it is known that they are not rumors. Also, as described in item B, the "Yi Sound Report" makes appropriate comments on matters that are subject to public criticism, or acts out of self-defense, and it can be known that it does not damage the plaintiff through fraud. After the defense statement, a counterclaim was also attached, with words the same as described in item B, also requesting that Wang Liwu be punished with Article 300 and Article 330 of the criminal law, and finally requesting permission to reserve the incidental private prosecution. Yesterday morning, Judge Wang Jianzu held a hearing to collect information. Lawyers for both sides presented evidence (newspapers). Then Wang Liwu made a statement, vehemently refuting the defendants' accusation that he had been expelled from the party, saying that he was not expelled from the party, but was not allowed to register, and that he had appealed to the higher party headquarters against the municipal party headquarters' disposition, and also said that the municipal party headquarters' announcement referred to his activities outside, and there were no words about swindling, etc. After successive arguments by the lawyers on both sides, Judge Wang immediately announced the verdict: Yu Jie'an and Hu Xiehou have nothing to do with the "Yi Sound Report," and are declared not guilty. Although Chen Moruo is the editor of "Yi Sound," the news published was transcribed from the Central Daily, so he is not responsible, and is declared not guilty. The counterclaim portion was dismissed for lack of evidence, and Wang Liwu was released without charge. After the verdict, Wang was still not convinced and shouted "appeal, appeal" incessantly.

Cigar Holder

Disguised as a Pistol ▲ Could Not Escape the Detective's Eye ▲ Real Pistol Frightened Off Bandits ▲ One Person Was Captured at the Time ▲ Sentenced to Five Years in Western Prison A probationary detective from the French Concession Police Station No. 125 was returning to his residence the night before last when, while passing near Route Pére Robert in the French Concession, three bandits, including Lu Xiudao, suddenly approached and blocked the detective's path, implementing their "slaughter the pig" principle, using a cigar holder as a pistol to prevent him from making any noise. The detective, seeing this situation, pretended to reach for his wallet and silver dollars, reached into his pocket, and pulled out a real pistol. Seeing the unfavorable situation, the bandits turned and fled. The detective bravely stepped forward, captured one of the robbers, Lu, and took him to the police station. Yesterday, he was sent to the French court for investigation. First, the detective took the stand and explained the situation and presented the defendant's fake pistol as evidence. When Lu Xiudao was questioned, he confessed to conspiring with the gang to rob, and stated that he had indeed committed a robbery with Zhang Heshang, who is still at large, on Route de Villermont last month. The Chinese and Western judges sentenced Lu Xiudao to five years in Western Prison for violating Article 370 of the criminal law, and to be permanently expelled from the Concession upon completion of his term.

Encounter with a Ghost at Night?

▲ The Accounts of the Two People Coincide ▲ There May Be Other Circumstances Involved Yin Linsheng, 24 years old, residing in Zhanghua Port Zhangzhuzhai, has been working as a mechanic at the Huangpu Engineering Department (i.e., the Dredging Bureau). At around 9 PM the night before last (the 21st), Yin was returning to Zhangzhuzhai from working the night shift at the bureau when, near the Zhanghua Port train station, he suddenly saw a person about five feet tall with very long hair, disheveled and draped over their shoulders, with a hideous face, jumping out of the darkness and rushing towards Yin. Yin, seeing this, suspected it was a bandit, was greatly alarmed, and immediately turned and fled, shouting for help. The Yin Xing Security Corps detachment stationed near the station heard the shout and immediately sent a team to rescue him. Seeing Yin running, they suspected he was a robber and immediately fired a warning shot into the sky. Yin, seeing a large team of Security Corps members arriving, became emboldened, immediately stopped, and explained the reason for his cry for help to the corps members. The corps members searched the surrounding area in all directions, but found no trace. However, they saw a man surnamed Zhang on the north side of the railway, burning paper money in front of his house. The corps members went forward to ask if he had seen anyone matching the above description passing by. According to Zhang, he was burning paper money to send away ghosts because a member of his family was seriously ill, and he had inadvertently seen a cloud of black energy rushing out of his house towards the door, and had seen a person in the shape described above walking in the black energy, and disappearing shortly afterward, presumably the ghost sent away from his house.

Page 16

The corps members, although Zhang's account matched Yin Linsheng's, found the account very bizarre and difficult to believe, fearing that there might be other hidden circumstances. They immediately escorted Yin to the Zhanghua Port Police Station of the Seventh District, First Branch of the Wusong Public Security Bureau for investigation.

A Scene of Con Artists Releasing White Doves

▲ Li Xiangsheng Borrows Money to Get Married ▲ Losing Both Wife and Money, He is Resentful Li Xiangsheng, 34 years old, from Funing, has been working in the Second Brigade of the Anti-Smuggling Camp. Although he is over thirty, he is still single. In December of last year, his acquaintances Chen Fengxiang and Zuo Shihong came and said that there was a widow, Shen Yan, named A Si, 23 years old, from Yancheng, Jiangbei. Her husband died early, her family was poor, and she had no means of support, so she had decided to remarry. Her appearance was very beautiful, but she needed to raise a dowry of 200 yuan to make it happen. Li was moved by the news and readily agreed. He borrowed 100 yuan from relatives and friends, and then set a date to sign a marriage contract in a certain teahouse. At the time, the matchmakers and the woman were all present to sign and affix their fingerprints. Li saw that the woman was indeed beautiful and was very happy. He took out the dowry of 100 yuan, exchanged it for the marriage contract, and took the woman home. He also made her beautiful new clothes and jewelry. Then he held a banquet to entertain guests. But Chen Fengxiang and Shen Yan were actually engaged in a scheme of con artists releasing white doves. Less than a month after the woman married into the family, she changed her mind completely. She knew that Li's monthly income was not very high, and he had no savings and a normal family situation. Since she could not extort much money from him, she decided to leave as soon as possible. On the 2nd of this month, she took advantage of Li's unpreparedness and secretly hid her jewelry and other items in her arms. She then made an excuse to go out to make tea, took a copper teapot, and left, never to return. When Li realized what had happened, he was both heartbroken and regretful. He had been deceived, but there was nothing he could do. He had to ask people to search in all directions. It was not until the day before yesterday that he received a secret tip from a friend that the woman was hiding at the home of Shi Shen, a woman from Taizhou, her little sister, at No. 954 North Chengdu Road in the Public Concession. At about 10 PM that evening, he went and arrested Shen Yan, i.e., A Si, and Shi Shen, and escorted them to the First Branch of the Municipal Public Security Bureau in the South City, requesting a thorough investigation and the recovery of the dowry and jewelry. The police chief conducted a preliminary hearing and ordered them to be detained separately pending investigation.

Suicide Due to Inability to Pay Rent

However, Xu himself owed the landlord four months' rent. The landlord repeatedly demanded payment without success and took Xu to the Fourth District Police Station. The police, stating that the case concerned rent arrears, advised the landlord to sue in court and refused to handle the matter. Although Xu was not imprisoned, the fact that he could not pay the rent remained a reality. Distraught, he hanged himself in his room the day before yesterday. His tenant, Jin Xueqing, attempted to rescue him, but it was too late. He reported the incident to the police station. Yesterday, the police ordered Jin Ertu and the local constable, Wang Shaoting, to report the matter to the District Court for verification. Inspector Lei and others arrived at the scene for inspection and confirmed the death as suicide by hanging. They instructed the relatives of the deceased to collect the body for proper burial, pending further investigation. However, as the deceased had no family members present, the body remained uncollected.

Fire Report from Lan Ni Du Yesterday Morning

▲ Investigation Reveals Kerosene and Alcohol

▲ Suspected Arson for Insurance Claim

Yesterday at 2:00 AM, a fire suddenly broke out upstairs at Xin Xie Shun Congee Shop, number 292, Dandanggong Alley, Lan Ni Du Street, Pudong. Thick smoke billowed out, threatening to spread. Fortunately, the Zhong family from Hubei, residing behind the shop, were hosting a wake for a deceased relative and were still awake. They shouted for help to put out the fire. Police officers Lang Shiquan and Shen Guangyun from the Third District Public Security Bureau heard the cries and rushed to the scene, sounding the alarm. Neighbors were awakened from their sleep and assisted in pouring water to extinguish the fire, preventing a major disaster. Police officers then went upstairs for inspection, discovering a basket of partially burned old cotton wadding with the smell of kerosene, as well as a jar containing a mixture of alcohol and kerosene. Upon closer examination, all items were determined to be accelerants. The shop owner was nowhere to be found, with only a shop assistant named Shi Kanglang present. Shi was taken to the district for questioning along with the evidence. Shi claimed to be 47 years old, from Chongming, and had been working at the shop since the first month of the lunar calendar. He did not know the owner's name, the cause of the fire, or the insurance amount. The district chief, upon reviewing the testimony, suspected the shop of arson for insurance fraud and ordered Shi to be detained temporarily. He also dispatched police officers to the Commercial Association to inventory the items in the shop and await summons for the shop owner to come for investigation.

Additional Details on the Fire in West Shanghai

Filial Daughter Follows Mother in Death

Yu Qingtang's home, number 9 Yu Geng Lane, south of Hongqiao Town, West Shanghai, was suddenly engulfed in flames on the evening of the 18th of this month when his mother, Yu Ding, accidentally knocked over a kerosene lamp, causing the fire to spread to nine neighboring homes, including Yu Bingsheng's, destroying more than twenty houses. Yu Ding failed to escape and perished in the fire, as previously reported. It is now known that Yu Ding's daughter, Wang Yu, who was over fifty years old, was heartbroken upon hearing the news of her mother's tragic death. She rushed to the scene and, among the rubble, found Yu Ding's charred body, the head and face severely burned beyond recognition. Wang Yu held the body and wept bitterly, fainting several times. She managed to have the body taken home, but suffered severe coughing and shortness of breath, dying soon after arriving home.

Careless Cake Shop Fire Kills Infant

Wang Qiaxing cake shop, opened by a Chongming native, at number 1 Taopeng Road, Yangshupu, suddenly caught fire yesterday afternoon at 3:45 PM. The fire spread to the adjacent small restaurants, destroying three houses. Wang's one-month-old infant was trapped by the fire and could not be rescued, perishing in the flames. The mother was also burned.

Passenger on the Nanyang Maru Commits Suicide by Jumping into the River

The Nanyang Maru, a Yangtze River steamer of the Nisshin Company, was traveling downstream from Hankou when a passenger named Tian Xianzhong, a 56-year-old from Daye, Hubei, suddenly jumped into the river unnoticed about five or six miles upstream of Datong. The captain, upon learning of the incident, immediately stopped the ship to attempt a rescue. However, by the time Tian was retrieved and brought to the deck, he was already dead. He had only two yuan on his person and no suicide note, so the reason for his suicide is unknown.

Shanghai-Changshu Ferry Robbed Mid-Journey

The Daji Wheel, belonging to the Shanghai Gongmao Steamboat Company, set sail from its dock at 4:00 PM on the 20th (the day before yesterday), heading to Changshu, Dangkou, and other places, towing several company boats. At about 11:00 PM that night, while passing the Panlonggang area of Zhuangjiajing, more than ten armed bandits suddenly appeared, firing a shot to force the driver to stop the boat. They stormed the company boat, threatening passengers and searching them thoroughly. They also approached the ship's purser, threatening him with a gun to force him to hand over money. After about an hour and a half, they fled with their loot, shouting triumphantly. The total loss is estimated to be over a thousand yuan. The ship's purser reported the incident to the local Public Security Bureau, requesting an investigation and arrest of the perpetrators.

French Water and Electricity Company

Reinstates Dismissed Workers

The French Water and Electricity Company had recently dismissed two workers, Dong Keguang and Zhu Asan, without cause. Subsequently, the Water and Electricity Workers' Union sent representatives Xu A'mei, Xu Mao'mao, Xu Shunsheng, and Zhang A'mao to negotiate with the company's foreman. Yesterday morning, at 6:45 AM, all the workers arrived at the factory, waiting to be allowed to enter and begin work. However, the factory manager, Barre, questioned the union's standing committee member, Xu A'mei, asking if they would be working today (i.e., yesterday). The workers replied that the time had not yet arrived. Manager Barre then went directly into the lathe room and closed the door, leaving the workers with nothing to do.

From 6:30 AM to 5:00 PM, the company intervened to resolve the situation. As a result, they agreed to reinstate Dong Keguang yesterday and Zhu Asan today, bringing the disturbance to an end.

Zhu Da Steals Pig, Falls into Cesspit

▲ Soaking Steamed Buns in Alcohol to Intoxicate Pigs

▲ Drowning a Pig Leads to Twenty Yuan Compensation

Ruan Qinxiang, from Jiangbei, who lives in a flat near Gujia Garden in Zhabei, makes a living by raising pigs. He had built a pigsty behind his house. When selling pigs last year, he kept two pigs unsold, to prepare for slaughtering when his second son, Xiaolong, married in March this spring. Unexpectedly, a neighbor named Zhu Da, having lost money gambling during the New Year, decided to steal Ruan’s two fat pigs to recoup his losses. He soaked a steamed bun in liquor, removed it after a while, and went to the pigsty late at night, throwing the liquor-soaked bun to the pigs to eat. Within minutes, the pigs were intoxicated. Zhu opened the pigsty and attempted to steal a pig and flee. However, there was a cesspit in the area, buried deep in the ground. Zhu panicked and fell into the pit, along with the pig. Fortunately, there was not much excrement, and he was not submerged. Unable to climb out of the pit, Zhu called for help. Ruan heard the cries and shone a light, recognizing his neighbor Zhu Da. He managed to help Zhu out of the pit, but Zhu was covered in excrement and smelled terrible. Ruan then discovered that one of his pigs had drowned in the pit. It was clear that Zhu had fallen into the pit while trying to steal the pig. Ruan negotiated with Zhu, threatening to take him to the police station. However, neighbors intervened and mediated, resulting in Zhu paying twenty yuan to compensate for the pig, settling the matter.

Attempt to Smuggle Opium Discovered

At the Shanghai South Railway Station on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway, at around 5:00 PM yesterday, a night passenger train No. 10 preparing to depart for Hangzhou was boarded by a person resembling a tea attendant, about twenty years old, carrying two large paper packages. He crossed the tracks from the back door of the station to the rear platform to board the train. The railway police at the station, noticing his panicked demeanor, approached him for inspection. The paper packages contained four pieces of opium, weighing 112 taels in total. The person and the opium were immediately detained and taken to the police station. The stationmaster was present, and the case was sealed with the station's stamp, before being sent to the District Court for interrogation.

Police Announce Claim for Lost Items

The Public Concession Police announced that they had recovered the following items: a silk-faced leather robe (half sheepskin, half another type of skin), and five yuan in banknotes. These items were seized from a robbery on Ningbo Road, Shilu Road, and Shanxi Road on January 23 of this year. Also, a gold ring and eight silver yuan, seized from a robbery on Sima Road on the night of February 9. If the owners can identify the items, they can go to the West Hongkou Police Station on Haining Road.

Meeting of the Board of Directors of Pushan Villa

The board of directors of Pushan Villa in Zhabei held a meeting at 5:00 PM yesterday at the main office, number 2, Six Malu Road. Directors Huang Hanzhi, Wang Yaolai, Yuan Ludeng, Zhang Xianqing, Chen Liangyu, Jin Yangfu, and Wang Junsheng were present.

After the usual formalities, Chairman Huang Hanzhi declared the meeting open, stating its purpose. Then, Director Wang Junsheng reported that in the past year, the villa had handled the burial of exposed corpses, burying a total of 29,247 large and small coffins in both the Chinese and Concession areas.

106 sets of bones were collected, and 10,643 large and small coffins were provided free of charge. The hospital had provided medical treatment and medicine a total of 41,758 times. He also proposed that the existing resting place was insufficient and that five more rooms should be built for storage. However, there was a lack of funding, and a solution needed to be found to remedy this. Mr. Chen Liangyu spoke, stating that Mr. Wang Junsheng had fulfilled his duties and shown great enthusiasm in handling burial affairs over the years, neglecting no effort. However, the scope of operations had expanded in recent years, requiring significant funds, which was a genuine concern. He requested all directors to assist in maintaining the benevolent cause.

Huang Hanzhi, Wang Yaolai, and the other directors agreed to discuss and plan ways to maintain the charitable undertaking, which was approved by all. The meeting adjourned at 7:00 PM.

First Day of the Third Exhibition of White Goose Art Institute

Yesterday marked the first day of the Third Exhibition of works by the White Goose Painting Research Institute, a renowned art group in Shanghai. The exhibition was held at the institute's new location, number 370 Changchun Road (south end of Dixuwei Road) on North Sichuan Road. Since the opening at 9:00 AM, people from all walks of life had been visiting in a constant stream. The venue was decorated in an elegant and refined manner, and the exhibited works were all carefully selected from the past six months. According to the person in charge of the institute, more than a hundred of the best works by the institute's researchers were unfortunately destroyed in a fire during the printing of the institute's annual publication, making it impossible for enthusiasts to see them at this exhibition, a regretful occurrence.

▲ Paint Trade Association The Shangda Paint Store, a member of the Paint Trade Association, and the paint department of Lihua Foreign Firm, angered the paint industry for violating the contract terms for ordering products, and negotiations were conducted in a serious manner. Now, the firm expresses willingness to compromise and has sent a letter requesting that the association mediate. The association accepted the request, and at 6:00 PM yesterday, a trial mediation meeting between the Chinese and foreign parties was held at Xinghua Building. Member Ma Shangjie and other members Shen Leshan, Li Shuyan, Zeng Yunlin, Ding Fang, and more than thirty others were present. Legal advisor Fei Guoxi, a lawyer, was also in attendance. The foreign firm was represented by the paint department manager Jin Dibeigen (translator) and staff member Luo Hanhe. First, the association's secretary, Wang Shipeng, presented the key points of the member's contract. Then, Li Shuyan discussed the principles of mediation and the direction of the treaty. After a lengthy debate between the two parties, the conclusion was reached that: (1) The Lihua Foreign Firm's representative promised to provide a concrete and satisfactory reply this Monday; (2) If the firm does not fully and properly comply with the agreement, the member will resolve the matter through legal channels.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory issued the following weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday: A low-pressure system is moving towards the northeast-east, approaching the area. There are cyclones over the East China Sea and the Yangtze River basin. There is heavy fog from Fujian to the Shandong coast. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in the area was 57.9 degrees, and the lowest was 48.9 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest temperature was 62.8 degrees, and the lowest was 39.5 degrees.

Shanghai Local Court

Education News

Important News

Ministry of Education Letter of Appointment

Experts for the National Education Conference The Ministry of Education has selected twenty-four experts for the National Education Conference, and appointment letters will be issued on the 22nd. Among them are Chen Heqin, an expert in early childhood education, Liu Enzhan, an expert in vocational education, Zhang Boling, a representative of private universities, Tao Zhixing and Tao Xuan, rural normal school teachers, Liao Maoru, a secondary education expert, Yu Ziyi, an elementary school expert, and Shi Weihuan, a Party Ideology Education expert.

A detailed list will be provided later.

Ministry of Education Recommendation

Wang Keren Appointed Supervisor of Students Studying in Japan Jiang Qi, the supervisor of students studying in Japan, previously had problems with the Party headquarters and requested to resign. The Ministry of Education dispatched Luo Qun, the manager of Guangdong students studying in Japan, to temporarily act as supervisor and appointed Zhu Baoqin, a counselor of the Ministry, to investigate in Japan. Now, according to Jiang Qi's written request to the Ministry, he sincerely requests to resign, and Luo Yiqun, due to poor health, is unable to take on the task and requests to be replaced by a formal supervisor. The Ministry of Education has appointed Wang Keren (a Guizhou native who graduated from the United States), the former principal of Wuxi Middle School and the current director of the Party Ideology Education Department of the Central Training Department, as the supervisor of students studying in Japan, and has reported to the Executive Yuan for approval and record.

Furthermore, it is reported that the affairs of the Supervisor's Office are becoming increasingly busy. The original organizational outline of the Supervisor's Office for Students Studying in Japan needs to be revised. Therefore, on the 15th, a request was submitted to the Executive Yuan to revise the organizational outline. The supervisor's position was originally a recommended appointment, but it is now changed to a simplified appointment. Under the supervisor, there were originally two section chiefs for academic affairs and general affairs, but now each section is changed to have one director and two staff members. It is heard that the expenses of the Supervisor's Office were previously 1,400 yuan per month, and the budget for the 18th year has been increased to over 2,000 yuan per month. However, this budget has not yet been approved by the Executive Yuan. As for the position of supervisor of students studying in Japan, the Ministry of Education has obtained Wang Keren's consent. Yesterday (the 21st), the official document recommending Wang to succeed as supervisor of students studying in Japan was sent to the Executive Yuan and will be decided after the administrative meeting on the 25th, and then appointed by the National Government.

Talk on Education Programs

The Compilation Committee of Education Programs of the Ministry of Education held a standing committee meeting at the Ministry of Education on the 21st in the morning and afternoon. The attendees were Standing Committee members Gu Shusen, Tao Xuan, Dai Xiujun, and Deputy Ministers of Education Liu Dabai and Huang Jianzhong, Division Chiefs Zhu Jingnong and Chen Jianxiu, Counselors Zhao Naichuan, Jiang Shaomo, and Zhu Baoqin, Secretary Zhou Gan, etc. Due to the lack of the required quorum (the Standing Committee requires four standing committee members to be present to hold a formal meeting, but only three were present: Gu, Tao, and Dai), a discussion meeting was held instead. The morning session, beginning at 9:00 AM, discussed the draft of the Overseas Chinese Education Program (this program was compiled based on the resolutions of the Overseas Chinese Education Conference convened by the Training Department of the Central Executive Committee in the 18th year and the Education Ministry's Work Allocation Table for the Period of Political Tutelage [Development of Overseas Chinese Education]). The chapters and sections of the draft, such as Chapter 1 on the goals of Overseas Chinese Education, various organizational provisions, various financial provisions, various accounting provisions, various school education provisions, and various social education sections regarding Overseas Chinese schools and students, were discussed one by one. Some were passed as is, while others were slightly modified, and the entire text was passed. The committee will then solicit opinions from various members by letter, and the committee will organize and decide. The afternoon session discussed the Higher Education Program, and only the full text of the plan to strengthen national universities was discussed and decided. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM and is scheduled to continue on the 22nd to discuss the unfinished Higher Education Program and the finalized version of the Secondary Education Program and the Social Education Program from the previous meeting.

Local

Municipal Education Bureau Orders Suspension

Private Surveying and Mapping Engineering College The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau is currently strictly cracking down on不良 private schools in the city. It has now been found that the private Surveying and Mapping Engineering College is poorly managed and has been instructed to suspend operations immediately. The order states that the college only has one classroom, the desks and chairs are messy and disorganized, and it is unclean and unusually dark. The person in charge of the college is always behind closed doors, and only a child of about ten years old who speaks Cantonese issues regulations from the window hole. There are no registered students, and the organization and equipment listed in the brochure are actually useless. The college is so poorly managed that it exaggerates in its brochures and other printed materials, behaving like a fraud. It should be ordered to suspend operations immediately. Recruitment advertisements and all printed materials must not be distributed again. This order is hereby issued for compliance and immediate suspension of operations to be reported. This order.

West-Qing Wins Championship – Yesterday's Results –

(A) West-Qing 49...East-West 32 (A) Qing-Guang 47...Friendship-Love 22

(B) Tu-Jin 72...Shang-Chu 17

(B) 33-33...3-Yi 23 The Shanghai Basketball Association held four group matches last night, two each in A and B. The West-Qing vs. East-West match was crucial. If West-Qing won, they would get the championship. If East-West won, there would still be an exceptional final match. As a result, West-Qing overcame East-West with a score of 49 to 32, thus winning the championship. Watching East-West's performance last night, it was quite lackluster. The guard Lu Zhongen was as steady as ever, but everything else was very flustered.

The forwards had no connection, and the score always succumbed to West-Qing, failing to show any promise. In the first half, West-Qing had 27 points, while East-West had only 14 points. At the beginning of the second half, the situation was still good, but then He Tong left the field due to a foot injury, and the strength became even weaker, resulting in defeat. The referee was Xu Zhendong, and the inspector was Shao Ji.

Xie Jin Association Seeks Far Eastern Games

Our Country's Athlete Badge The Chinese National Sports Association announced: When the International Games are held, the representatives of various countries use either the national flag as a badge, or the special products of each country as a badge, or objects made of national colors as a badge.

All are sufficient to indicate the marks of each country and express its special spirit. The 9th Far Eastern Games will be held in Tokyo, Japan, starting on May 24th. Our country's athlete badge intends to solicit public opinion and select the best to strive for perfection. The main points are listed below. We hope that the people of the country will find a way to design and grant us instructions. (1) Must use national colors; (2) Sufficient to express our country's four thousand years of culture; (3) The pattern must be clear and beautiful. Applicants must send it to this association by March 15th. Late submissions will not be considered. Once adopted, a small reward will be sent to express gratitude. The first place will be rewarded with 30 yuan, the second place with 20 yuan, and the third place with 10 yuan. Those that do not meet the requirements will not be replied to.

Yesterday's Group A Match

Lehua Wins Against Navy ▲Result: Two to One ▲Performances Were Terrible Fuyi, Lehua team, with its temporary talent, and the Navy team, with its flat and incapable skills, are in a contest, and it can be seen that its soldiers and horses are strong, promoting martial arts and showing off power, sweeping thousands of troops, and dominating for a time. Who knew that in the ninety minutes of fighting, the Navy's momentum was initially weak and then strong, while Lehua's sharpness was initially strong and then weak. Fortunately, Captain Li made contributions first, so that the entire team did not fail completely. Otherwise, the future of the Group A championship would be unimaginable. What is hoped for from Lehua in the future is that, regardless of the size of the battle, regardless of the strength of the enemy, they should rely on their individual strength and the spirit of the entire team to move forward aggressively and work hard. If they win, it is gratifying, and even if they lose, they will have honor. Hopefully, they will not underestimate the enemy and become arrogant, and tend towards disappointment, as they did yesterday.

On this day, Kang Haner, a sailor from Zhongshui, played for the Navy. He was burly and good at fighting, but his skills were mediocre and not surprising. The previous shooting was not at all sure, and the rear defense was even more chaotic. If Lehua could exert its full strength and show its prowess, then this small pawn would not be worth looking forward to. Among the Navy's eleven players, the best was Zhonglu Kais, whose solo charge to seize the base was the reason for not losing completely.

▲Lehua Team Lineup

Chen Bingxiang Li Shouhua Chen Lin Li Huitang Zhou Xianyan Sun Sijing Dai Linjing Li Ning An Yuansheng Chen Jiaqiu Xi Qiaosheng ▲Navy Team Lineup Shi Shentuo Ao Pei Er Shi Maoertou Qiao Po Laya Kais

Pei Tuo Meng De Fei Jia Zhuanzheng ▲A Thunderclap on Flat Ground Referee Ke Pu blew the whistle, and nearly ten thousand spectators craned their necks and looked forward. Thousands of eyes followed the ball. Initially, Lehua started the battle against the wind, advancing deeper. Soon, the army counterattacked, but retreated without effect. Then, Zhong Dai Linjing obtained the ball and passed it to Li. Li Huitang played a trick, confusing people's ears and eyes, changing from left to right, and went straight to take it. His left foot rose and shot into the left side of the goal. A thunderclap on flat ground shocked all the Chinese and Western men and women in the garden, and they cheered endlessly.

▲A Dose of Stimulant The victory and defeat of the two teams were already clear, and the situation became flat. Lehua learned that the opponent's skills were limited, so they used their skills, applying their own tricks, tilting to the left and right, as if playing with them in the palm of their hands, playing between their legs. The desire to advance decreased, and the ambition to strive weakened, so that in the back-and-forth, there were few surprising performances. The audience in the garden, as if entering a sleepy village, almost regarded the athletes of the two teams as playing children's games. Thirty-five minutes of good time passed in the blink of an eye. At that time, Li Huitang made a comeback, advancing lightly and quickly, cleverly avoiding enemies all the way, breaking through difficulties with wisdom, running unimpeded, leisurely and comfortably. Finally, the figure and the ball entered the net at the same time. Then, thousands of spectators, as if taking a dose of stimulant, applauded and shouted, rising from all sides, to express their elation. In the first half, Lehua two, Navy zero. ▲Great Disappointment from the Audience After changing formations and fighting again, Lehua, with the help of the wind, first launched a strong attack. Li Huitang picked from the side to the center, passing through the crowd. Xi Qiaosheng took over, kicking up a foot, but with weak strength and weak momentum, it was blocked by the goalkeeper. Left winger Shi Weituo attacked the ball and went straight along the line, passing a ball in the middle. Zhou Xianyan suddenly rushed up to capture it. If he had been a little negligent, Zhonglu Kaen had been prepared, then within five steps, there would have been a disaster. Great is this move, and together with Li Huitang, they were the heroes of Lehua's victory that day. Afterwards, Lehua's internal and external troubles arose repeatedly, either suffering from exhaustion or being injured and unable to walk. The entire team gradually had a gloomy scene, lacking a spirit of revitalization. Looking back at the Navy, it was like the rising sun, with thousands of sights. The trend of the army, the momentum of ten thousand, was due to the loss of shooting, wasting opportunities. In addition, Zhou Xianyan's defense was tight, with no opportunity to take advantage of. Otherwise, Lehua's supreme honor would have been destroyed in one fell swoop. However, the Navy repeatedly attacked and always worked hard. In the last ten minutes, they finally got their due reward. Zhongfeng Kaen went deep into the enemy alone, having gone through several lines of defense, and scored a goal. After this, Lehua's storms continued, but fortunately Li Ning, Sun Sijing, Chen, Li Huitang and others worked hard to persevere, and managed to maintain the final result of two to one victory.

Laugh It Off

— Sea Guest

Child—Mother, is this bottle of water?

Mother—Oh. No, it isn't. This is glue.

Child—No wonder I put on my hat and can't take it off ▲Wife (playing chess with her husband)—Do you know today is my birthday?

Husband—Is it?

Wife—Yes. Do you have any gifts for me?

Husband—Of course. I'll win this game of chess for you.

▲Woman (asking a firefighter a lot of questions)—May I ask what the leather belt you're wearing is for?

Firefighter—Madam. If we encounter women who like to talk incessantly, and we're tired of answering, this belt can be used for our jawbone to rest on.

▲Customer in a barber shop—Why do you always like to tell ghost stories when you're cutting hair?

Barber—Because it makes your hair stand on end, so my scissors can easily cut it off.

▲Fashionable Lady—I heard noises in the house last night.

There must have been a thief.

▲Miserly Husband—It must be because you bought a pair of expensive dancing shoes yesterday, so the thief came to steal them that night.

Mr. Wu Zhihui's Interesting Anecdotes Upon Arriving in Changzhou

— Wen Gui

Mr. Wu Zhihui, an important figure in the party and the country, came to Changzhou on the 18th as the officiant for the marriage of his cousin, Ms. Ke Xiu, and Zhao Liancheng. Here are some interesting anecdotes that were recorded.

After Mr. Wu arrived in Changzhou, he toured the streets for a week and then stayed at the Huashang Hotel, using the pseudonym Wu Hanqing. In the evening, a friend, Zhu Zhongchao, sent a news reporter to visit. Wu refused to meet them. The friends repeatedly requested from across the door. Wu replied that he had already gone to bed and had completely taken off his clothes. If you have anything to say, talk tomorrow, I can't open the door.

On the morning of the 19th, Mr. Wu went to the eastern suburbs to visit Tianning Temple and Wenbi Pagoda. At Tianning Temple, he saw a monk angrily questioning a monk and beating him severely. At the top of Wenbi Pagoda, he wrote an article titled "Old Tricks from Sixty Years Ago," which contained many interesting anecdotes, detailing how the monks of the temple should not be so bureaucratic and how the Bodhisattva should be sad, etc. This article was handed over to Fan Baizhu, a reporter from the Zhongshan Daily, for publication.

When asked whether Mr. Wu was from Changzhou or Wuxi, Wu replied that he grew up in Wujin, so of course he was from Wujin. However, he speaks with a Wuxi accent, so he can be said to be from Wuxi. He has lived in Shanghai for more than ten years, so he can also be said to be from Shanghai. In short, in terms of nationality, I am a Chinese. After saying that, he laughed loudly.

Mr. Wu's speech at the wedding was full of wit and humor. He briefly stated that he had come to Changzhou today to say a few words in Changzhou dialect. The Zhao family of Daixi Bridge and the Wu family of Xueyan Bridge are old relatives.

Now they have formed a new relationship. In the future, I hope they will continue to form relationships.

Zhao Liancheng has studied abroad for many years and has also studied well. My cousin's scholarship is excellent, so she was named Ke Xiu. It can be said to be a happy marriage. Now everything is progressing. People from the countryside also come to the city to get married. Heneige, people from the countryside, come to the city to get married. This is something to be proud of.

I just said I was going to speak Changzhou dialect, but I can't say it. Now I can only mix Wuxi, Changzhou, and Suzhou dialects to say it. Today, the Wu family's and the Zhao family's two families are getting married. I still have a blessing to say, which is "Many sons and many grandsons."

After Mr. Wu finished his business, he went to the train station at 5:00 PM that afternoon to leave. He first bought two train tickets for Shanghai and Nanjing. When catching the train, it was the 5:15 PM down train. It was probably going towards Shanghai.

Mr. Wu and his friend Duan Mengtao talked about airplanes. He said that he had flown twice. Before the first flight, he thought it would be difficult to fly. In fact, it is not much different from being on the ground.

It is also very stable after sitting, and you can write or walk on it. I flew, and Hu Zhantang scolded me. He said that he always thought that you Wu Zhihui had flown ten years ago. Unexpectedly, you are only flying for the first time today, etc. There is also a type of airplane that costs 50,000 US dollars, which is equivalent to 100,000 yuan in Chinese currency. It can hold ten seats, has a rest area, and has a writing desk. This type of airplane.

I once advised Chiang Kai-shek to buy one. For example, if you want to go to Guangzhou, you can get there in ten hours.

Talking about Fengyang, the Relics of Hongwu

— Wang Dingjiu

Fengyang is a household in northern Anhui. It is the hometown of Emperor Zhu Yuanzhang of the Ming Dynasty. There are many scenic spots and beautiful stories. Fellow member Mr. Wu has been teaching in Fengyang for seven years. Last year, he returned to Shanghai for vacation.

The members of the society held a banquet for him in a restaurant. At the table, we talked about the story of Hongwu.

There is much to record. Therefore, I write to tell the readers of Free Talk.

▲Huge Iron Woks Three miles outside the North Gate of Fengcheng, in the fields, there are five incomparably huge iron woks. According to legend, there were years of famine due to war. There was famine in northern Anhui. Emperor Ming cared about the people's difficulties, so he ordered officials to set up porridge here for disaster relief. The iron woks were used to cook porridge. It is said that each wok of porridge was enough for 500 people to fill their stomachs. From this, it can be seen how huge its volume is. Legend has it that a novice monk from a certain temple was watching by the wok when cooking porridge. He accidentally fell into it. At that time, everyone was at a loss. After three days, the porridge in the wok was exhausted, and a pile of white bones was found at the bottom of the pot. It was heard that a novice monk had also disappeared from a neighboring temple. Only then did they know that he had suffered this tragic death.

▲Closing the Door Is Already Daybreak Hongwu came from a commoner background. He lost his parents at a young age. He was once a monk at Huanglong Temple. The temple is a large temple in Fengyang. The temple is magnificent. According to legend, the temple occupied more than 100 acres during the Ming Dynasty. There were dozens of gates. The mountain gate was locked at night. This was done in order to sequentially lock towards the back gate. When entering, Ming was the head. When exiting, the east was already white. The scope was so wide. The temple has suffered since Hong Yang. Only one-tenth of what remains today exists.

▲Hongwu's Sword Millet in Front of His Mother's Tomb Hongwu's tomb was built in the capital. It is based on Purple Mountain, sharing immortality with President Sun. His parents' tomb is in his old hometown. It is six miles from the city. There are many northern things in the north. It is everywhere. When Hongwu was a swaddling infant, his mother spread diapers on it. He felt the sword millet prick his hand, so he said angrily. Why not face down for the convenience of people?

What is the reason for looking up? After saying that, the sword millet faced down. The matter was heard by the public.

Everyone was surprised. Then they realized that Hongwu was no ordinary person. Later, he became emperor.

Hundreds of years have passed. In the land of Mingling, the sword millet that grows there all has its thorns facing down. This is also an oddity.

The New York Telegram of the 21st Reported the Cotton Market Situation for the Past Week: Observing the actions of the cotton market, it can be seen that until the issue of new cotton acreage is resolved, the industry and cooperatives will likely not provide active assistance above a price of 1.06 yuan. This situation can be further seen in the increase in sellers when yarn prices rose slightly this week. There were indeed several companies that bought at limited prices every day this week, but in general, this type of buying only occurs when prices fall. There is better news regarding progress in agricultural work, and there is also an indication of increased fertilizer sales. In addition, wheat prices are weak. These are all reasons for the decline in cotton prices. Promotion to reduce cotton acreage is still underway. However, although cotton farmers have been warned not to overproduce cotton, they are still tending to increase cotton acreage due to hopes that the Agricultural Bureau will protect cotton prices. Therefore, many believe that this trend still needs to be overcome through promotion. Also, demand for spot cotton is slow, other goods are falling in price, and cotton cloth transactions are sluggish. It is expected that American cotton consumption will greatly decrease. Government actions remain uncertain. Due to these several factors, speculation is scarce. Caozhou Anecdotes

— Cheng Zhizheng

Caozhou is located west of Jining. Since ancient times, it has been a place contended for by military strategists and a shield for Shandong Province. My friend, Qian Ziyuanru, once served as the director of academic affairs at Liuzhong. Upon his return, he spoke in detail about the situation there. I will briefly record it to inform the readers.

Caozhou was a prefecture during the Qing Dynasty. However, upon arriving there, one sees barrenness everywhere. The streets are strangely narrow. The city is not even as good as the larger cities in Jiangsu Province. The local customs are fierce. Many of the people are skilled in martial arts. The strongman performances that we see in Shanghai are amazing.

In Caozhou, this is nothing extraordinary. Once, a soldier clashed with a student. Several soldiers attacked the student together, but they were defeated by him and fled like rats.

Many residents of Caozhou have a smoking addiction. Five or six out of ten shops in the market sell cigarettes. Most of them smoke the Hademen brand. The annual consumption is truly alarming. The currency used for transactions is mostly double copper coins. One silver dollar can be exchanged for three thousand cash. The cost of living is very low, so expenses here are extremely low. The most important products are fruits, such as pears and peaches, which are large and sweet. Each piece costs only twenty or thirty cash. There are many fruit trees. Guests can pick and eat them without interference, but they cannot take them away. If they could be transported to Shanghai, the price would multiply. In Caozhou, men and women still adhere to the ancient custom of not touching hands when giving or receiving. When women walk on the road, men are not allowed to stare at them. Those who are slightly inattentive will be beaten by the crowd. Those who arrive there for the first time often do not know this, so many people are beaten. When entering a country, one must ask about its customs.

The residents are simple, honest, and quick to learn but slow to acquire wealth. They greatly respect teachers. Every morning at five o'clock, one can hear the sound of reading. Persimmon frost, a type of local product, is extremely effective in treating hemorrhoids.

Where Did the Wild Mandarin Ducks Fly From?

— Lan Yin

The other day, at the home of Huan Liu in Mingxing Lane, Gonghe Road, Zhabei, a pair of unfamiliar wild mandarin ducks were found in the downstairs厢房, enjoying a good dream. The downstairs 厢房 was rented by a carpenter named Chen. Chen goes out to work every day and does not close the door. On this day, Huan Liu returned from buying groceries and suddenly saw the door of the 厢房 tightly closed, which aroused her suspicion. She peeked through the crack in the door and discovered a man and a woman sleeping together. She called the police to arrest them. It is truly a rare and absurd story that wild mandarin ducks would dare to enter someone's house for a secret rendezvous. Unexpectedly, there was another similar incident. Yesterday, at the Hua family's home on Gongping Road, a similar situation occurred. The Hua family lives in the front building with only a husband, wife, and daughter. The husband works at a company and leaves early and returns late. The wife is addicted to mahjong and spends her days visiting neighbors to play. The daughter is still young and likes to stay with her mother. At that time, the wife was strolling in the bamboo grove and instructed her daughter to guard the house. Before long, the daughter also left the house to join her mother. When they returned after the game, they found the door locked from the inside. They were shocked and screamed. Inside the room was a pair of wild mandarin ducks, floating in bliss between life and death. Hearing the noise, they were also startled. They hurriedly opened the door, and neither the man nor the woman was recognized. They looked at each other in astonishment, their faces flushed with the warmth of spring.

The expressions in their eyes and eyebrows told a story. The wife could not help but make a scene. The wild mandarin ducks were even more embarrassed. Amid the shouting and scolding, a certain man surnamed Mou, who rented the back building, returned from outside. The man rushed to him. Mou asked in surprise what was happening. The man stammered that he had entered the wrong room and begged for help. It turned out that the man and Mou were from the same hometown. One day, they met on the road, and the man learned Mou's address. He had brought his mistress to visit him, but mistakenly entered the front building. For a moment, they were overcome with desire due to lust and laughter, thinking that Mou was a good friend and had not brought his family to Shanghai. They thought it would be fine to temporarily enjoy a moment of pleasure. Who knew that it would turn out to be such an embarrassing scandal? In the end, Mou mediated and ordered them to light candles and burn incense in the room to ward off bad luck, and the matter was settled. Compared to the wild mandarin ducks in Zhabei, who were sentenced to fifteen days of detention by the police, they got off easy.

Clever Dog

— Ji Jin

My neighbor, surnamed Zhu, has a dog. It is very clever.

It always tries to please its master. One day,

the dog suddenly developed an eye disease. Pus filled its eyes, and it was about to go blind. The family hired a doctor to treat it. The doctor said, "I'll try treating it with medicine for humans first. If it doesn't work, I'll try a better method." So, he had the dog lie down beside him and applied the medicine. The medicine was strong, and the dog barked wildly in pain, but it did not run away. After a while, the condition improved greatly. The next day, the doctor came again. The dog wagged its head and tail, as if expressing joy and gratitude. Then, it lowered its head to the doctor, just like a human. After the medicine was applied, it lingered and looked around, not leaving for even a short distance. It waited until the doctor left and escorted him to the door before stopping. This happened three or four times. Everyone praised it as a clever dog.

European Travel Correspondence (42)

— Liu Haisu

▲ The Death of Bourdelle

Three, His Art (Part 2)

Rodin created "The Man in Action" and "The Thinker." He loved to use strong, nervous muscles, realizing them in the movements of his sculptures. It seems to be a kind of "power" and "thought," its radiant aura shining throughout the universe. His sublime and magical talent, along with the powerful expressiveness of his human figures, lifted him above the major flaws in his own art. Many of his students only wanted to make themselves strange and peculiar, and thus they committed these serious mistakes, merely changing the form while lacking any substance. Even the materials used for sculpture were completely ignored. These signs of decline inspired Bourdelle to pursue the permanence of ancient civilizations. From Michelangelo, he realized that the sculptor's task was not to carve a beautiful exterior but to create solemn and powerful forms from rough stone. Therefore, after long deliberation and exploration, Bourdelle finally made new discoveries. He paid great attention to the materials of sculpture without being confined by them. While pursuing new forms of expression, he also carefully avoided their dangers. Rodin also did not hide his admiration for his talented student.

"Bourdelle seeks 'truth' through relentless reasoning, abandoning the old for the new without hesitation or regret. His works are extremely rational. Every detail has its reason for existence and important value in the whole. There are no accidental discoveries, no repetitions, and no awkward parts. His lines are precise and composed, not because of a lack of talent but because of his synthetic necessity." You see, this is his evaluation of his technique. There is nothing more to add or argue about. However, Bourdelle is not like other "constructivists." He does not suppress the excitement of emotion; he only knows how to control it.

Bourdelle was influenced by various sources, but he always maintained his own identity. He transformed the forms he gained from Rome, Greece, Babylon, and Egypt through his own mind. Because of this, he was able to combine the movement of modern art with the sanctity of Aegean culture, the greatness of the Renaissance, and the tranquility of Olympia. On this point, great artists are a thousand times greater than glorious warriors who die on the battlefield. Because war gives us the impression of hatred, while artists leave behind works that inspire people to know more about gratitude, love, and beauty. True beauty shines among the stars and can never be erased.

Common Sense Snippets

— Chi Fo

When carrying a large amount of money, you should wear shabby clothes. I have seen young people become proud and arrogant,

showing off huge wads of cash when shopping, not realizing that it could lead to a deadly disaster. Being robbed is a minor matter. During this period of late books, when buying books at large bookstores such as the Commercial Press, you should go when they first open at nine in the morning; otherwise, you will have to wait a long time.

Exchanging silver dollars near a streetcar station will definitely cause you to lose a few copper coins.

Buying cheap goods on the street will guarantee that you will be swindled. Buying cigarettes on a ship will guarantee that you will get fake goods.

If you are not greedy for wealth or beauty, no matter how dangerous the sea is, you will never fall into the trap.

The Confused and Unclear Silver Loan Market ▲Market Overview The price of silver loans fluctuates with the difference in supply and demand. A slight delay causes it to fall, and a slight advantage causes it to rise. Although it cannot be considered a spiral trend, a state of confusion and uncertainty is undeniably the reality. For example, yesterday's market first rose and then fell, and the difference was minimal. People's minds remained indecisive, with inconsistent views on whether to be bullish or bearish. In reality, there is no opportunity for rapid growth at present, but there is also no ability for a sharp decline.

▲Silver Loan Prices In the early market, sentiment was quite bullish, so temporary asking prices were mostly above two cents. However, with sellers unwilling to act, the result was a soft market, so the closing price was 71.9875 cents, a decrease of 0.0125 cents compared to the previous day. The fluctuations were minimal, and trading was normal. The supply of silver for loans remained abundant, with no worries of depletion. The market remained loose. The market price for borrowing, bank rates, and the rates for big accounts were not announced.

Fluctuating Gold Prices

▲Fluctuating Around 490 Taels Yesterday was Saturday, and gold trading was only conducted for half a day in the morning market. The gold market fluctuated up and down, but ultimately softened. Overall, it was difficult to break the spiral trend, and it remained around the 490 tael mark, with fluctuations of about four taels. The opinions of those in the industry were divided and uncertain, and trading was not active. It was difficult to buy large quantities, and it was also not easy to sell if there were many sellers. Regarding foreign exchange, the rate was raised by one level, but internally it was stable. Some in the industry sold, and the gold market initially fell in the morning due to the high rate for large amounts. Later, buyers seemed eager, and prices rose steadily, breaking through the 490 tael mark. However, at noon, sellers became active, foreign exchange eased, and the market atmosphere was poor, abruptly cutting two taels, with the final price at 489 taels.

the US dollar increased by 500 cash, and the Nikkei rate decreased by 100 cash, which did not cause much movement. The rate was 488 taels 900 cash. Suddenly, the trend seemed to rise, and the foreign exchange rate improved. The Nikkei Silver Company bought 1.02125 taels in April and also bought British gold at 11/64. There was also buying of the Zhengjin rate until it reached 490 taels at 10 o'clock. At this time, some retail accounts sold, and the price decreased by one tael. After 10:30, banks traded British gold for May at 11/64. The buying sentiment seemed strong, rising steadily. At 11:15, it rose to 491 taels 200 cash. Later, the Dalian gang and Zhifeng Yong and others sold. The Nikkei rate softened, and it was not easy to sell long-term Nikkei at 1.02125 taels. Therefore, the gold price broke through the 490 tael mark again and suddenly fell to 489 taels 200 cash at noon. The closing price was 489 taels 300 cash, a rebound of 400 cash compared to the previous day.

Foreign Exchange: Apparently Weak, Actually Strong

Yesterday was Saturday, and foreign exchange trading only took place for half a day in the morning. The HSBC exchange rate increased by one level. The British exchange rate increased by 25 to 1 shilling and 1.5 pence, the US dollar increased by 500 cash to 47.625 yuan, India increased by 1.5 yuan to 131 rupees, France increased by 13 yuan to 1,216 yuan, and Germany increased by 2.5 yuan to 199.5 marks. Japanese currency increased by 1.25 yuan to 118.5 yuan, the Po currency decreased by 100 cash to 118.5 taels. The Japanese exchange rate decreased by 100 cash to 1.03375 taels. Hong Kong remained at 80 taels. Overseas telegrams reported that the Indian exchange rate increased by 1.06 rupees to 49 rupees, and there were no rises or falls in Yokohama and Kobe. The market was sluggish.

As for the internal market of local banks, various exchange rates were still stable. The market was slightly depressed in the morning,

but it tightened again as the gold price rebounded. By noon, it seemed to loosen, but the gold price had already fallen back below 490 taels. However, compared to the previous day, there was a slight improvement, with the British rate decreasing by .0625, the US dollar decreasing by 25, and the Japanese exchange rate increasing slightly by .0625. Regardless of whether the trend was apparently weak or actually strong, people's minds were uncertain, almost inversely proportional to the previous day. Some Chinese speculators sold slightly, with about 50,000 to 60,000 pounds of British currency sold. Banks were willing to buy, with Zhengjin, Tonghui, Shanghai, and Shiye making purchases. Banks also traded 20,000 to 30,000 pounds and 100,000 US dollars. As for the Cantonese gang, Shengda and others sold more than 100,000 yuan, which was purchased by Mitsui and Toa. The Japanese exchange rate was sold by the gold industry for more than 1 million yuan. Banks that bought included Sumitomo, Taiwan, Mitsui, Mitsubishi, and Tonghui. The Dalian gang sold several hundred thousand yuan to the current Dalian to hedge the gold price. However, the result was quiet.

British and American Silver Prices Both Rebounded

According to telegrams from London yesterday, the price of silver bars had both rebounded. The near-term rate increased by 1.875 to 20 pence, and the long-term rate also increased by 1.875 to 19.875 pence. Both China and India bought, but trading was not high. According to telegrams from New York, the price of American silver also rebounded by 0.375,

to 43.25 cents. The British rate against the US increased by .0625, and the US rate against the British remained unchanged at 4.8615625 yuan. The Japanese rate against the US remained unchanged at 49.1875 yuan, and the British rate against the Japanese increased by 0.03125 to 2.03125 shillings. The British rate against Shanghai remained unchanged at 2 shillings. Also, Reuters reported at 11:00 AM today that there were no increases or decreases, and the Dentus news agency reported that there were no changes.
